I looked like I had smallpox. A top of the line moisturizer is the key to making this system work, imo. I saw results within a week, and now my skin is ALWAYS clear. If I don't wash my face at night (I wear Mac Studio Fix) I may get a very small blemish that quickly goes away with regular cleansing/maintenance. My skin is also BALANCED for the first time ever. It isn't oily nor dry nor combination. Just soft and balanced. I find that the cleanser runs out very quickly - much faster than the other products ( I only use the toner and lotion - not the mask or anything else by proactiv) - so I use it at night, and use another scrub I like, Aubrey Organics Jojoba Meal and Oatmeal Mask and Scrub with Rose and Lavender for Dry Skin, in the morning. It really, really softens and brightens your skin. I've also found that since using the proactiv and lush moisturizers my acne scars have faded FAST. I bought a skin lightening gel on ebay, but I haven't needed to use it. I'm very please with this system, and I hope it never stops working for me. I don't know what I'd do. This has been the only cure for my acne, which I believe might be hormonal. Do not use this system without an excellent moisturizer and expect good results. What don't I like about these products: the packaging. The bottles are ugly and cheap looking. But the ingredients do produce results. Eventually I was able to stop using doxycycline and my skin has remained clear. I never worry about acne now, and it's such a relief and a blessing. I totally wasted large sums of money at the dermatologist. A+++

  9. I first started suffering from acne when I turned 14 and hit puberty. I went through a delayed puberty so when I first started breaking out (small blackheads and whiteheads around my nose); I didn't know what to do. I am now 19. In the 5 years that I've been suffering from acne it has progressively exacerbated. It reached a peak around 15 and 16. I was a sophomore in high school and I had a terribly low self-esteem. I hardly ever had eye contact with my teachers or classmates because I was so embarrassed of myself. It did take a huge toll on my social life because it totally killed my self-esteem as a person. I can't quite remember when Proactiv Solutions started to become very popular, especially during 2005 or so when it started to become increasingly popular through advertisements. I will sit in front of my TV and ponder if it really did work like magic as the long commercials made it seem. Proactiv was advertised very strongly through the use of pathos and by providing testimonies of different patients that truly made it seem like it had changed their lives. To an extent, I have to admit I started to feel somewhat brainwashed concerning the effectiveness of this product. (Crazy how much advertisement can affect you psychologically). It wasn't until late in my sophomore year of high school when I finally decided to give Proactiv a try. I had nothing to lose, really...just a few bucks. When I finally got the kit delivered at my house I was overjoyed with happiness. I read through the booklet that was included and started to use it as the directions stated. At first I felt like I had put all my hope and faith into this one product but after a few weeks of use, I started to realize it really wasn't as magical as a lot of the commercials made it seem. I'm going to be very frank with you...Proactiv might seem to work at first but after repetitive uses it will start to lose efficiency. For the first 2 weeks or so, my acne definitely got better: blackheads started to dissipate and I also lost sight of most pimples. After a month or so, my acne started to gain control over the medication. It no longer worked as well as it did the first few weeks and I felt I had been shot in the leg once again. My faith in Proactiv started to decrease and I became frustrated with the medication in general. What bothered me the most was the fact that Proactiv only works if you use it consistently: Twice a day and every day of your life, really. Even Proactiv itself states how you have to use this product on a daily basis. I'm not a very diligent person so the 3 step therapy that Proactiv requires started to become annoying. I found it extremely cumbersome having to wake up early in the morning to go through the entire 3 step therapy, and then setting aside some time to apply it before going to bed. The second step was the most annoying one because you have to wait until the cleanser (Revitalizing Toner) dries before you can apply the repairing lotion. After I realized that Proactiv was starting to lose effectiveness, so did my diligence began to crumble. I'm now 19 and I must confess that Proactiv has been somewhat of a disappointment for me. I have learned over 5 years how to cope with acne and minimize it, but I have not completely found a cure or \\"secret recipe\\" to fight it completely. My acne has definitely improved since high school, but it hasn't gone away completely. Proactiv is one of those products that only works as well as commercials and testimonies declare for only a very specific audience. I feel that this product might not be for you if you suffer from hereditary and chronic acne (this is my case). If you are one of those people reading this review and still pondering whether or not you should buy it, I will first take a step back and consider what kind of acne you have... If you have moderate to mild acne, this product might work perfectly for you. I'm going to be veryfrank, I've met some people that have truly loved this product because it works for them. It might not work for you. The efficiency of this product depends on many factors. One of them is whether or not you can keep up with it... Buying a kit every month or so can turn out to be very costly, especially for a person that cannot afford paying $44 + S&H every time you run out of supply. Another factor is how consistent you are with applying the product properly. You have to be extremely diligent about it while simultaneously maintaining a healthy lifestyle (eating right, exercising, maintaining high hygiene standards, etc.) A huge part of getting rid of acne depends on the effort of the person and how well you balance your life. The last and most important factor is the type of skin you have as well as the severity of your acne. If you suffer from moderate acne, which is what a lot of teenagers and adults have, this product will work wonders for you. I won't completely dismiss the fact that through advertisement Proactiv has gained a reputation on being one of America's greatest antidotes for acne. Most people by now know about it and the brand itself is becoming iconic concerning today's society about being among the most popular treatments for acne. I personally find it a bit overrated concerning it's effectiveness. Acne is something that most people encounter in their lives at least once and that's probably the reason why Proactiv has become so popular, especially among those individuals that are extremely conscious of their image. Also, although the commercials make it seem that Proactiv is not harsh on your skin, it actually is. I have relatively resilient skin and I have used much more stronger medications to cope with my acne and I must confess that Proactiv does make my face itch and burn after the application of the repairing lotion. Vulnerable areas like around the lips and eyes can react very sensitive to this medication. For many, this product might be a painful experience using it as it does burn (especially during the first few applications before your skin gets used to it completely.) The reason why I gave this product 3 stars for my evaluation was because it does seem to work better than most over-the-counter products that are out there. Like I said, it does work for some people but it might not work for you. If you are one of those people that suffers from hereditary acne, I think I will consider investing in other much stronger medications like Accutane or something in that form that can combat acne from the inside. Acne is predominantly caused and controlled through internal factors such as the chemistry of your body which include your oil production and the fluctuation of your hormones (these are the two predominant factors that affect acne; aside from genetic inheritance.) I personally can't afford Accutane but I have consider trying it in the future despite the known side effects (liver damage, possible depression, etc.) I have heard extremely positive commentaries from the people that have tried Accutane which is currently the only medication that can really cure acne. Although it is a 6 month treatment and it must be under strict observation, it does seem to have extremely favorable results for those that undergo it. I think for those people that do suffer from severe acne it is better to fight acne from the inside with oral antibiotics like Accutane, instead of just attacking acne from the outside. As I mentioned earlier, acne is triggered because of your chemistry, so attacking acne from the inside seems more rational to me than just applying it directly on to the skin where it can only do so much. If you suffer from moderate acne and acne does not run in your family, I will definitely consider this product. It certainly has a lengthy research history and it is definitely an \\"above average\\" acne product when you compare it to other much inferior products thatyou find in today's stores like Neutragena, or Clearasil. By the way, I have also tried AcneFree, which can be considered the corollary to Proactiv and it is definitely a lot stronger (in my opinion). You can get it through Amazon as well and it is slightly more affordable than Proactiv Solutions. It has a similar net effect on your skin as Proactiv, however. You must use it consistently and there's a possibility your skin might grow immune to it pretty rapidly. Acne is one of those things that takes part of most people's lives and this product will always be among the most well known medications to control it. If you can afford this product, use it consistently and as indicated, and keep in mind buying this product for the next decade or so of your life before acne starts to become less evident, then buy it. Otherwise, I wouldn't because it will only be a waste of money and acne will keep becoming a persistent force in your life. Bottom line: If you suffer from mild acne, I will totally recommend this product. However, I will keep in mind the statements I have mentioned above before buying it. If you suffer from almost incurable and persistent acne, I wouldn't put too much trust in it. It might work but there's also a chance you might end up with a similar story as me. Good luck.

  132. Though Proactiv Solution works pretty well for me, I have never seen a product vary so drastically from one user to another. I started getting terrible acne in the 9th grade, and it had a major effect on my confidence. People would stare at my zits--and not into my eyes--whenever we were having a conversation, and my 10th grade history teacher even held me back at the end of class specifically to recommend a skin care product that she had ordered from Avon. If that were not embarrassing enough, my acne reached a peak during my senior year of high school--the primetime of every young woman's life. Every inch of my cheeks was covered in bright red, pus-filled pimples. It was so terrible that some people looked disgusted to even stand near me, and I had to wear a TON of concealer for my senior photos--which only exacerbated the problem as soon as picture day was over. After my high school graduation, I started spending a lot of time out at the pool, and (despite what the experts say), the sun drastically improved my skin. My face turned really red one day when I forgot the sunblock, and the next day, all of the zits were gone. However, when the summer ended and I went to college in the fall, the zits came back. It was then that I decided that I need something stronger than an over-the-counter medicine to deal with my skin. After watching a commercial for Proactiv Solution, I ordered it over the phone on a whim. The first few weeks didn't give me any results, but after a about a month, the product worked to its full potential. I have been using it for almost two years now, and I am very happy with my decision to purchase it. Though it has not provided the magical results that are showcased in every commercial (I still get a couple of pimples every couple of weeks, my face is not the horrible red mask that it once was. Unlike some reviewers reported, the product does not dry my face out at all, and I haven't experienced any redness. The most redeeming product of the entire system is the toner. Though it does not smell very potent, it succeeded in removing from my hands and forearms a botched application of self-tanning lotion that almost a week of constant scrubbing did nothing to help. For me, this is very good stuff. Unfortunately, as I stated, this product varies so widely from customer to customer that it is hard to determine the effectiveness of its use. In my circle of friends, three girls (myself included) are using Proactiv. My skin reacted very nicely to the product, but the other two weren't as lucky. One of the girls had mild acne and experienced no change in her condition. Another girl had moderate acne and experienced such severe burning and redness of the skin that she discontinued usage and even voluntary went through the seven levels of Hell (also known as Proactiv Customer Service) to get a refund. Overall, here are my basic recommendations for those considering using Proactiv: 1.) Since results vary so widely between each user, buy the smallest amount of the product that is available. That way, if it does not match your particular needs, you are not out an arm and a leg on something totally useless 2.) Beware of the freebies/extras. The basic three step Proactiv system and the Daily Oil Control lotion work wonders (compared to the \\"before\\" situation), but the other items in the Proactiv line were actually pretty damaging. As a \\"free gift\\", I received a tube of the Refining Mask. I applied it according to the directions, but approximately twenty minutes after I removed it, my face was covered in large red, itchy blotches. I immediately threw the tube in the garbage, and by the time I resumed using my regular system the next day, the spots were gone. So, if you get extras in the mail, proceed with caution. 3.) DO NOT, under any circumstances, tell the representative that you want a free month's supply VitaClear Vitamins with your purchase. First of all, the vitamins are disgusting. VitaClear comes in abox with thirty individually wrapped packets of 5 vitamins. After taking that first packet of five vitamins one morning, I had to make a run to the restroom to vomit. The next day, I had didn't throw up, but I did a second time after using the vitamins a few days later. Though I followed the direction to eat before usage, no matter how much or how little I ate, I would puke at least twice a week. If this is not enough, as soon as you agree to accept a free order, you (unknowingly) sign yourself up to receive auto-shipments of Vitaclear every two months--which means that your credit card will automatically be charged $29.99 every six or weeks. I have no idea how to cancel an account with VitaClear (which is sold by a different company than Proactiv). The only reason I stopped receiving shipments was because I changed addresses and my credit card just happened to expire that same month. So, if you like swallowing five vitamins each day that will make you puke, feel free to sign up for auto shipments of a product that is impossible to cancel. 4.) As I mentioned previously, Customer Service is Hell (according to the people I know who have tried to cancel). If you want to cancel your account, you have to locate the customer service number from the website or from your previous bill. Proactiv does not allow easy online cancellations or (to my knowledge) mail-in requests to cancel. Then, when you call a representative and mention that you want to cancel your account, you are mysteriously put on hold for an indefinite amount of time--though they jump at the chance to talk to you if you are willing to order Proactiv. If you are not put on hold, the reps will talk in circles and try to convince you to order more products. One of my friends who successfully canceled her account recommended setting up a web count on the Proactiv site, going to the help feature, and then emailing a representative with the question \\"How do I cancel my account?\\" A rep contacted her by email afew days later, asked for her account number, and subsequently canceled the account. I recommend following this procedure or continue to receive the automatic shipments each month. Overall, this product worked for me, but it will not work for everyone. It is kind of like spinning the Wheel of Fortune or flipping a coin...only this time, instead of head and tails, the sides are \\"Clear Skin\\" and \\"Not\\".

  147. My teenaged son has had a bad case of acne for more than a year now. We've tried a variety of different medicines, one of which actually made his acne worse!<br /><br />It seems like nothing we tried worked, so after hearing several friends recommend Proactiv, we decided to take the plunge and buy a 2-month supply, even though it's a little expensive. After using it for several weeks now, we've seen a very slight improvement in our son's acne, but nothing major.<br /><br />We finally got fed up with all of the over the counter stuff and decided to visit our pediatrician. He told us that our son had 3-4 level acne on the Pillsbury scale which classifies the severity of acne from 1 to 4. Our doctor said that what's in Proactiv isn't really that much different than what's in most of the other over the counter products. He also said that the main reason people who used it showed some improvement is because it motivated people to be regular in their acne hygiene routine - something teens are notorious for not being faithful with.<br /><br />What's more, apparently the latest research shows that in severe cases of acne there is bacteria under the skin that must be treated by antibiotics and that treating it superficially isn't likely to help much. So now we're moving from using Proactiv to using prescription antibiotics and some stronger prescription acne medicines.<br /><br />Wish us luck!<br /><br />If you have a less severe case of acne, then Proactiv might be for you: the main thing is to use it consistently. But if you have a severe case, it's not likely to help very much, and you'll probably have to get a prescription for something stronger.

I was determined not to have to deal with this problem at this age. I had seen Proactiv commercials and was hesitant to start it. I did not realize that it was a subscription-based plan at the outset. Either I just did not read the information on the site carefully enough or it wasn't that obvious. Either way, I decided that I needed something so I would try it.<br /><br />I will tell you that it has been about 2 months and my skin has never been this clear. Granted, the effectiveness of a product may depend on the person and the kind of acne they have but I can honestly tell you the my skin is more smooth and more clear than it has EVER been. I do get an occasional pimple now and then so it is not a cure. They tell you that acne cannot be cured -- only controlled. Even so, I don't get pimples very often now and if I do get a pimple, it is dealt with right away and effectively. I added the refining mask which seems to be very effective in dealing with the occasional bump. I am very happy I bought it. I do have a few dark scars from acne but the product does not claim to remove scars. It does claim to even out skin tone from the discoloration that can accompany break outs. Right now, my face is tan from summer so it is not so obvious and my acne scars seem to fade anyway on their own in time so I am not terribly worried aboutthem. But,aside from those three or four scars, my skin is wonderful.<br /><br />As far as the horror stories I am reading here about cancelling it are concerned, I can't say except my niece was using it for a while and she liked it very much. It worked well for her also and she suffers from acne worse than I did. But she could not afford it any more so she cancelled it and I never heard that getting out of it was an issue for her. I don't plan on stopping it since it is working for me so well but I guess I will find out at some point how difficult it will be to cancel the subscription. I suspect that if you tell your bank to deny any further payments to them, they will stop it quickly enough because I cannot imagine they will continue to send you product if they are not getting paid.<br /><br />So, that is my story. So far, I love the product. It works very well. If you wear make up, they tell you to get a foundation that has the acne medicine in it. I did this even though I don't wear make up very often, when I do, it has the medicine in it which helps because the medicine sits on my face all day that day. Anyway, it was worth it for me.
